- You cannot enter blocked cells.

- If a move is invalid, you remain in place.
- At most ONE agent may occupy the corridor at one time.
- If both agents attempt to enter or occupy the corridor at the same time, a corridor conflict occurs.

- The world is a 7 by 5 grid. 
- A narrow horizontal corridor exists at row y=2. 
- The corridor cells are [(2, 2), (3, 2), (4, 2)].

- A2's goal: (0, 2)

REWARD STRUCTURE:
Reward rules:
- Each step including waiting has a cost.
- Reaching your goal improves your reward
- Each invalid move or movement conflict costs you more than ordinary.
- A corridor conflict results in a penalty for both agents.

**10 most important points**

1. **Open the Find dialog** – Press **Ctrl + F** (or **Ctrl + H** for Replace) to bring up the Find/Replace pane.  
2. **Enter the search term** – Type the word or phrase you want to locate in the “Find what” box.  
3. **Navigate results** – Use **Find Next** (or the arrow keys in the pane) to jump to each occurrence.  
4. **Search scope** – Click **Find in** → choose *Main Document*, *Selection*, *Headers & Footers*, etc., to limit where Word looks.  
5. **Whole‑word and case‑sensitive options** – Check **Match whole word** and/or **Match case** to refine the search.  
6. **Replace functionality** – In the Replace pane, type the replacement text in “Replace with” and use **Replace** or **Replace All**.  
7. **Formatting search** – Click **More** → **Format** → *Font*, *Paragraph*, etc., to find text that has specific formatting.  
8. **Wildcard search** – Enable **Use wildcards** to search for patterns (e.g., `he?l?` finds “hello”, “help”, etc.).  
9. **Troubleshooting** – If Word can’t find text, check that the correct scope is selected, that formatting options aren’t unintentionally restricting the search, and that the document isn’t protected or in a different language.  
10. **Combine with Navigation pane** – Use the Navigation pane to view all headings and quickly jump to sections, then use Find to locate specific text within those sections.
